  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_13b26ab1-df40-469b-82b6-145ad8487eb2'

      $('rating_details').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer13741353283221200212"><b>One Life to One Dawn.</b><br/><br/>In a land ruled by a murderous boy-king, each dawn brings heartache to a new family. Khalid, the eighteen-year-old Caliph of Khorasan, is a monster. Each night he takes a new bride only to have a silk cord wrapped around her throat come morning. When sixteen-year-old Shahrzad's dearest friend falls victim to Khalid, Shahrzad vows vengeance and voluntee</span>
  <span id="freeText13741353283221200212" style="display:none"><b>One Life to One Dawn.</b><br /><br />In a land ruled by a murderous boy-king, each dawn brings heartache to a new family. Khalid, the eighteen-year-old Caliph of Khorasan, is a monster. Each night he takes a new bride only to have a silk cord wrapped around her throat come morning. When sixteen-year-old Shahrzad's dearest friend falls victim to Khalid, Shahrzad vows vengeance and volunteers to be his next bride. Shahrzad is determined not only to stay alive, but to end the caliph's reign of terror once and for all.<br /><br />Night after night, Shahrzad beguiles Khalid, weaving stories that enchant, ensuring her survival, though she knows each dawn could be her last. But something she never expected begins to happen: Khalid is nothing like what she'd imagined him to be. This monster is a boy with a tormented heart. Incredibly, Shahrzad finds herself falling in love. How is this possible? It's an unforgivable betrayal. Still, Shahrzad has come to understand all is not as it seems in this palace of marble and stone. She resolves to uncover whatever secrets lurk and, despite her love, be ready to take Khalid's life as retribution for the many lives he's stolen. Can their love survive this world of stories and secrets?</span>
  <a data-text-id="13741353283221200212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>

<a href="/questions/473705-i-really-want-to-read-this-book-but-the">I really want to read this book but the cover makes me feel ill!! Anyone else feel the same way? It&#39;s the holes! :(</a>
</div>

<ul class='questionFooterActions'>

<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_473705'><a id="like_count_community_question_473705" rel="nofollow" href="/rating/voters/473705?resource_type=CommunityQuestion"><span class="likesCount">68 likes</span></a>&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;<a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F18798983-the-wrath-and-the-dawn">like</a></span>

<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/2972600-nidhi-bhatt"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1567109152i/2972600._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/2972600-nidhi-bhatt">Nidhi Bhatt</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Actually the holes are an important part of Arab and Moghul Architecture as the females are to be kept in veils. the windows from which female members<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">‚Ä¶more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Actually the holes are an important part of Arab and Moghul Architecture as the females are to be kept in veils. the windows from which female members of the royal families used to see outside the Royal Palaces used to have all these intricately carved designs through which they could view everything going on outside. They are called "Jarukha" in Hindi language. The people outside could not see inside the Palace or if there is anyone standing on the other side of the window. :)<br /><br />The cover just depicts the Main Character behing such window. Such Jarukhas are really famous in Moghul Palaces in India.<br /><br />I hope this helps... :D<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1283811149" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1283811149" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1283811149?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-as-good-as-i-expected">not-as-good-as-i-expected</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=boooring">boooring</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=watch-out-for-puddles-of-angst">watch-out-for-puddles-of-angst</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=cheesy-cheesy-cheesy">cheesy-cheesy-cheesy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=derp-moments">derp-moments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dishonor-on-your-cow">dishonor-on-your-cow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=dragged-on-too-much">dragged-on-too-much</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=girl-squad">girl-squad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=not-worth-the-hype">not-worth-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=bye-bye-nineteenth-amendment">bye-bye-nineteenth-amendment</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1283811149" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16864255282521946281"><b>1.5 stars</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"How can I desire him? After he killed Shiva. After he killed so many young girls, without explanation. <br/><br/>What's wrong with me?"</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><u>A three-sentence summary of The Wrath and the Dawn:</u><br/><br/>Shahrzad: I will kill Caliph Khalid to avenge my best friend!<br/>Khalid: *eye smoulder*<br/>Shahrzad: Lol, nah. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446123281ra/16751481.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>That is literally what happens. I'm not joking. <i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i> is a retelling of the classical One Thousand and One Nights tale. Every day, the Caliph of Khorasan marries a new bride and by dawn, he </span>
  <span id="freeText16864255282521946281" style="display:none"><b>1.5 stars</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"How can I desire him? After he killed Shiva. After he killed so many young girls, without explanation. <br><br>What's wrong with me?"</i>
</blockquote><br><br><u>A three-sentence summary of The Wrath and the Dawn:</u><br><br>Shahrzad: I will kill Caliph Khalid to avenge my best friend!<br>Khalid: *eye smoulder*<br>Shahrzad: Lol, nah. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446123281ra/16751481.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That is literally what happens. I'm not joking. <i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i> is a retelling of the classical One Thousand and One Nights tale. Every day, the Caliph of Khorasan marries a new bride and by dawn, he has her killed. Shahrzad marries him to get revenge for her best friend and within three days, she's putty in his hands. <br><br><b>Three fucking days.</b> Where's the fire? Where's the hate? Where's her <i>brain</i>?<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"It's because he's not the monster I thought he was. <br><br>There was so much more below the surface, and she had to know what lay at the root of it all."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>The book tries so hard to convince readers Shahrzad is Katniss by making her a master archer and spout promises for vengeance. But <b>it'd be nice if she actually <i>carried through with her plan.</i></b> Her attempts at sniffing out Khalid's weaknesses are poorly thought-out and completely disappear after she falls in insta-love with sunlight-scented Hay Boy. I mean, Khalid. <br><br>There's a scene where she directly confronts Khalid on why he kills his wives and he leaves because she has the subtlety of a hippo in a tutu. She then spends the whole day fretting she hurt his <i>feeeeelings</i> and apologizes. Apologizes. For wanting answers. For demanding an open relationship. For understanding why her best friend had to die.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1445550236ra/16669375.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm confused to what the intended message is. <b>That if you stick it out long enough in an abusive relationship, you can change him?</b> That violent jerks with short tempers are precious cinnamon rolls with hidden depths? <br><br>Keep in mind Shahrzad falls for Khalid <i>before</i> she discovers the real reason behind the murders (in which he's totally blameless because God forbid he's a morally grey character). She is in love with someone who murdered her best friends and hundreds of other girls. At one point, she calls him her "beautiful monster". <br><br>Young girls are reading <i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i> and forming their idea of love from it. Do I need to say how dangerous that is? Isn't <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10818853.Fifty_Shades_of_Grey__Fifty_Shades___1_" title="Fifty Shades of Grey (Fifty Shades, #1) by E.L. James" rel="nofollow noopener">Fifty Shades of Grey</a> enough?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446123281ra/16751482.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Speaking of Fifty Shades, let's address the elephant in the room: <i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i> is the Arabian <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>. There's insta-love like I mentioned and a love triangle with Shahrzad's childhood friend Tariq. Khalid is a gorgeous male specimen who's secretive, hates himself, and a brilliant fighter. He even has amber eyes.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446123281i/16751483.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Another thing that bothered me are the rape scenes. <b>Their marriage consummation and the night after was rape, okay?</b> Just like Drogo and Daenerys' marriage was built on rape. Shahrzad <i>didn't</i> want it. She just went ahead with it to earn Khalid's trust. (Edit 29/6/2020: Even if you argue it's technically not rape because she seemed physically willing, it's definitely not fully consensual and thus rapey.)<br><br>Later, we discover Khalid had never entered any other bride's bedchamber except hers. Which begs the question: Why? If he loved her from the start, which he does, <b>why would he violate her like that?</b> Why would he perform on her one of the cruelest crimes you do to a person? Or is it supposed to be romantic and special because she's the exception? That's a prize I don't ever want to fucking win.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1389814071ra/8056603.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then there's the plot itself. Or should I say lack of plot. For a story about murder and mind games, it is surprisingly slow. Nothing really happens until the climax, which abruptly cuts off just when the story ball starts rolling. They cheated me out of a decent climax. Most of the storyline is devoted to the romance, people traveling, and descriptions of clothes.<br><br>So. Much. Descriptions.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"She was dressed in wide silk trousers and a fitted top stained a deep violet color, with think straps that banded over each shoulder. The necklace and thin chain at her waist contained amethysts surrounded by tiny, pale pink diamonds. At her ears and along her brow were large teardrops of purple and gold."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>I estimate 25% is describing what Shahrzad is wearing at any given time. There are a lot of foreign terms, too. Not just for clothes, but weapons and titles and such. Qamis, sirwal, shamshir. I appreciate the research that went into writing this, but there's a point when it gets annoying. It feels like the author is showing off instead of telling us the damn story. The writing itself is overblown and jammed with unnecessary metaphors.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1446123281ra/16751484.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>By far the worst YA book I've read in a long time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16864255282521946281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_932203967" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/932203967" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/932203967?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer932203967" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6842535673171682301"><blockquote>
  <i>She wanted to kiss him.<br/><br/>No.<br/><br/>It was one thing to return his kiss; she‚Äôd been prepared for that. But it was another thing entirely to want his kiss . . . another thing entirely to desire his affections. To melt into the arms of Shiva‚Äôs killer at the first sign of adversity.<br/><br/>Weak.</i>
</blockquote><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431462006ra/14839196.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Retellings should light my imagination on fire. They should take the original story, add a twist to it, make it so that we don't feel like we're reading the same old, same old. The only twist, <b>the only imaginative reimagi</b></span>
  <span id="freeText6842535673171682301" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>She wanted to kiss him.<br><br>No.<br><br>It was one thing to return his kiss; she‚Äôd been prepared for that. But it was another thing entirely to want his kiss . . . another thing entirely to desire his affections. To melt into the arms of Shiva‚Äôs killer at the first sign of adversity.<br><br>Weak.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431462006ra/14839196.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Retellings should light my imagination on fire. They should take the original story, add a twist to it, make it so that we don't feel like we're reading the same old, same old. The only twist, <b>the only imaginative reimagining to this book is the addition of a fucking love triangle and the rewriting of the should-have-been mysterious, brilliant, Scheherazade into an astoundingly stupid chick.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1418356766ra/12754883.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Scheherazade of the original <i>1001 Nights</i> is a woman to be admired. Brave, smart, fearless. She used her intelligence to survive when countless others have died, enchanting the king by weaving tales so mesmerizing that the king could not bear to kill her. This book's main character <b>Shahrzad</b> doesn't hold a candle to the original.<br><br>Seriously, there was no point to this book. I could have read the original and been satisfied, because there was very little variation. We have a king who marries a woman and kills her after their wedding night. We have a main character who tells stories. She really does tell stories. I swear it felt like 1/4 of the book was devoted to the story she tells. <br><br><b>It was astoundingly dull.</b> I didn't read a retelling to read yet another freaking rendition of Aladdin, among other tales. Spare me, please. I don't need to summarize what happens because everyone knows what the premise is. Insane motherfucker gets wronged in some way. Decides to marry a girl and kill her the next morning for some weird reason because COMMON SENSE Y'ALL. Girl decides to sacrifice herself like a sheep to the slaughter by marrying the dude herself, and secretly plots to stave off the executioner's axe by telling him a story and leave it on a cliffhanger every night. And the truth? I don't know why she's not dead. I don't know why he lets her live. Her charms are entirely hidden to me. I cannot comprehend the attraction she holds. Her stories bore me to tears.<br><br>I digress, but isn't that so intensely annoying? As book lovers, don't we hate cliffhangers? If I were the king, I would have just strangled her myself instead of waiting the next night to hear how the story ends. <b>IMAGINE 1001 NIGHTS OF CLIFFHANGERS.</b> DIIIIIIIIIIIIIIIE BITCH.<br><br>D:<br><br>The main character is stupid. So dumb. She talks big, fo' sho. She's all like I WILL KILL THE KING!!!!! I WILL AVENGE MY FRIEND'S DEATH AT THE HANDS OF THE MURDEROUS MONSTER.<blockquote>
  <i>‚ÄúWife.‚Äù He nodded.<br>‚ÄúMy king.‚Äù<br>I will live to see tomorrow‚Äôs sunset. Make no mistake. I swear I will live to see as many sunsets as it takes.<br>And I will kill you.<br>With my own hands.</i>
</blockquote>And then like literally 2 days later she feels a pull on her heartstrings when he glances at her.<blockquote>
  <i>I despise him.<br>She tried to ignore the flutter of uncertainty in her stomach.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1431462006ra/14839197.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She is so dumb. Like she has ZE GRAND PLAN TO KILL THE KING (as previously stated). Only it fails pretty miserably. You see, in order to form a competent plot, <b>
  <i>you can't fucking reveal your hand</i>
</b>. WHICH SHE DOES. Like showing that she's a highly accomplished archer...<b>because surely knowing she can kill will make the Caliph feel so safe with her.</b> Fucking idiot.<blockquote>
  <i>She exhaled slowly.<br>As soon as she opened her eyes, she loosed the arrow. It flew toward the target in a perfect spiral.<br>And struck exactly where she intended.<br>‚ÄúAmazing. Despite never taking care to aim, you actually hit the target that time,‚Äù Jalal intoned drily. ‚ÄúIn a fashion.‚Äù</i>
</blockquote>She's defiant. She takes unnecessary risks, given her plot. I can't headdesk hard enough.<br><br>The love story is absolutely atrocious and unbelievable. There's not only ZE GRAND LOVE TRIANGLE between her childhood friend...<blockquote>
  <i>Tariq continued, the silver in his eyes flashing. ‚ÄúBut understand this: no matter how many perfect young women you put in my path, there is only one Shahrzad.</i>
</blockquote>But there's also zero chemistry between the main character and the <s>murderer</s> love interest. A love interest who is pretty fucking smart and vigilant.<blockquote>
  <i>His eyes, which were usually vigilant, appeared even more watchful than before.<br>She sighed to herself.<br>He notices everything. This will be even more difficult than I thought.</i>
</blockquote>Which begs the question...<b>
  <i>why her?</i>
</b> Why this stupid, incompetent, bumbling fool of a revenge-seeker?<br><br>So, my dear friends, <b>don't hop a carpet and fly to this Arabian night.</b> Because this book's main character is more of...<blockquote>
  <i>A fool off his guard<br>Could fall and fall hard<br>Out there on the dunes</i>
</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6842535673171682301" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1109539517" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1109539517" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1109539517?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1109539517" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7421264554019054599"><b>
  <i>‚ÄúMake sure they never forget. You are the Calipha of Khorasan, and you have the ear of a king.‚Äù She bent forward and lowered her voice. ‚ÄúAnd, most important, you are a fearsome thing to behold in your own right.‚Äù</i>
</b><br/><br/>My original plan was to finish this book tonight and then write up a review tomorrow, but after that ending, I just can't stop thinking about it and I need to get my thoughts down right now. In short: I enjoyed this book very much. Way more than I expected to, to tell the truth. And </span>
  <span id="freeText7421264554019054599" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‚ÄúMake sure they never forget. You are the Calipha of Khorasan, and you have the ear of a king.‚Äù She bent forward and lowered her voice. ‚ÄúAnd, most important, you are a fearsome thing to behold in your own right.‚Äù</i>
</b><br /><br />My original plan was to finish this book tonight and then write up a review tomorrow, but after that ending, I just can't stop thinking about it and I need to get my thoughts down right now. In short: I enjoyed this book very much. Way more than I expected to, to tell the truth. And I guess you should know that, though there are many elements of fantasy and action, it is primarily a romance. And yet...<br /><br /><b>It completely melted my cold, unromantic heart.</b><br /><br />Where should I start? <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn__The_Wrath_and_the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath and the Dawn (The Wrath and the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath and the Dawn</a> was a deliciously angsty, sexy romance inspired by <i>A Thousand and One Nights</i>. If you know me, you know how often I complain about romances - either the guy's a jerk, the girl's annoying or they fall into some crazy instalove that just leaves me bored. Well, I finally found a romance where I just loved the characters, totally obsessed over what would happen, and finished the final page with a pounding heart.<br /><br />My god, what has this book done to me?<br /><br />This story is about Khalid, the Caliph of Khorasan, who takes a new bride each night only to have her executed at sunrise. When Shahrzad's friend becomes the Caliph's victim, Shazi volunteers herself with a plan to outwit the evil ruler and exact revenge. In a similar way to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/331830.Keturah_and_Lord_Death" title="Keturah and Lord Death by Martine Leavitt" rel="nofollow noopener">Keturah and Lord Death</a>, Shazi extends her date with death by telling Khalid a story and promising only to reveal what happens next if he should let her live another day.<br /><br />As it turns out, of course, nothing is as it first seems and Khalid is hiding many secrets. The relationship between the two develops from seething hatred (on Shazi's part) to reluctant companions to something much more. I've been craving a romance that feels genuine in its development and actually has me wondering how things will turn out (and, god help me, the jury's still out on that last point). The dialogue between them is addictive and feels natural... <b>and don't you just love stories within stories?</b><br /><br />Though I said this book is primarily a romance, there are many other things that need mentioning. There are some beautiful descriptions of the palace, for one thing, and a wonderful cast of secondary characters that all feel important to the story and not just throwaway. Jalal is charming and hilarious, Despina is a source of much-needed female friendship for Shazi, Yasmine is intriguing and bitchy (but kinda in a good way) and Tariq inspired a mixture of love/hate feelings in me.<br /><br />Sure, it's not a perfect book. I definitely think Shazi didn't try so hard to get her revenge and missed a bunch of opportunities, and I was a little frustrated with how long it took Khalid to trust her with his secret. But, oh well.<br /><br />If you're partial to a bit of romance, then hear me out. A book which contains lines like the following and manages to make me swoon instead of rolling my eyes must be something kind of special:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>‚ÄúMy soul sees its equal in you.‚Äù</i>
</b><br /><br />and<br /><br /><b>
  <i>‚ÄúWhat are you doing to me, you plague of a girl?‚Äù he whispered.<br />‚ÄúIf I‚Äôm a plague, then you should keep your distance, unless you plan on being destroyed.‚Äù The weapons still in her grasp, she shoved against his chest.<br />‚ÄúNo.‚Äù His hands dropped to her waist. ‚ÄúDestroy me.‚Äù</i>
</b><br /><br />God, I love the two of them. And I need book two.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7421264554019054599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_813320250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/813320250" />
    <a title="Wendy Darling" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling"><img alt="Wendy Darling" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379959930p2/2745288.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/813320250?book_show_action=true">Jan 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Darling" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Darling" href="/user/show/2745288-wendy-darling">Wendy Darling</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer813320250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7613203744862919886">Hm. People are loving this much-hyped book, but I have rather mixed feelings about this one. <br/><br/><b>Things I liked:</b><br/>-- awesome premise, obviously<br/>-- a world very different from what we're used to<br/>-- a few intriguing conversations between women (Shazi and Despina, Shazi and Yasmine)<br/>-- diversity, yay<br/>-- a few nice action scenes towards the end<br/>-- the romance, which eventually sparked and got me very invested in what's going to happen next!<br/><br/><b>Things I wanted more of:</b><br/><br/>-- Magic (perhaps this will come in the next bo</span>
  <span id="freeText7613203744862919886" style="display:none">Hm. People are loving this much-hyped book, but I have rather mixed feelings about this one. <br /><br /><b>Things I liked:</b><br />-- awesome premise, obviously<br />-- a world very different from what we're used to<br />-- a few intriguing conversations between women (Shazi and Despina, Shazi and Yasmine)<br />-- diversity, yay<br />-- a few nice action scenes towards the end<br />-- the romance, which eventually sparked and got me very invested in what's going to happen next!<br /><br /><b>Things I wanted more of:</b><br /><br />-- Magic (perhaps this will come in the next book)<br />-- Complexity of emotion<br />-- development of character, particularly in secondary ones<br />-- showing versus telling (the writing feels a bit...mannered?)<br />-- less glossing over/quickly moving past important scenes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[such as consummation of their union. It's fine if it's not explicit, but to relegate this major life-changing event to a couple of sentences--particularly when she gives this as sacrifice for the greater good--is incredibly disappointing. No internal narrative or emotional reaction? Really? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />-- more interesting recounting of The Arabian Nights. I mostly skimmed those parts, tbh, since we were already told so much of the main story, and Shazi's "telling" of the tales didn't have a unique spin/evocative writing/subtext<br />-- explanation for why the two main characters are drawn together, particularly why Khalid is so intrigued by Shazi that he continues to spare her life. <br /><br />Honestly, I was keenly interested throughout this entire story, but I didn't feel particularly swept away by it, or moved until closer to the end. Until the last few chapters, the whole thing needed more complexity and subtlety and subtext and mystery. When there's finally an outpouring of emotion, however, followed by the scenes when everything's finally on the table and the betrayal and sacrifice as a result of that? That's when the story catches a little fire and made me genuinely invested in the characters, and anxious to see what happens to them. Here's hoping the sequel continues the momentum and delivers in the promise implicit in the last few chapters of <i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i>. <br /><br />Okay, 4 am ramblings are at an end. I will probably come back and tinker with this a bit to finish it off.<br /><br /><i>An advance copy was provided by the publisher for this review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="7613203744862919886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1326850187" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1326850187" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1326850187?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1326850187" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6329006839360692249"><b>I loved it beyond words.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473283893ra/20440956.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I'm in awe. This beautiful journey, this journey of <b>longing, magic and love</b> sang to my soul, gave me wings, spilled vibrant colours in a bleak routine and made my heart burst.<br/><b><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4600197.Renee_Ahdieh' title='Renee Ahdieh' rel='nofollow noopener'>Renee Ahdieh</a> is a rare storyteller.</b><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‚ÄúOne hundred lives for the one you took. One life to one dawn. Should you fail but a single morn, I shall take from you your dreams. I shall take from you your city.<br/>And I shall take from you these lives, a thousandfold.‚Äù </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>The Caliph of Khorasan, the King </span>
  <span id="freeText6329006839360692249" style="display:none"><b>I loved it beyond words.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1473283893ra/20440956.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm in awe. This beautiful journey, this journey of <b>longing, magic and love</b> sang to my soul, gave me wings, spilled vibrant colours in a bleak routine and made my heart burst.<br><b><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4600197.Renee_Ahdieh" title="Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Renee Ahdieh</a> is a rare storyteller.</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‚ÄúOne hundred lives for the one you took. One life to one dawn. Should you fail but a single morn, I shall take from you your dreams. I shall take from you your city.<br>And I shall take from you these lives, a thousandfold.‚Äù </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>The Caliph of Khorasan, the King of Kings, is a monster. <br>Every day he takes a new wife. And every dawn, he executes her. One of those unfortunate girls was Shahrzad's best friend. Blinded by her grief, her hatred and the desire for revenge, Shahrzad volunteers to become the Caliph's next wife, with one goal in mind; destroy him. Kill him and rid Khorasan of a bloodthirsty tyrant. When the dawn comes and she's still alive, the speculations begin. Why did the Caliph spare her? Is it possible that the monster has a heart after all? And indeed, the enemy turns out to be just a boy, a boy with the weight of his sins on his shoulders. Torn between her promise for revenge and her traitorous heart, Shahrzad might be the only one that can make Khalid care again. But what is the cost?<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‚ÄúI will live to see tomorrow's sunset. Make no mistake. I swear I will live to see as many sunsets as it takes.<br>And I will kill you.<br>With my own hands.‚Äù </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>When I started <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath___the_Dawn__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath &amp; the Dawn (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</a> I was cautious. Later, I was fascinated but a little detached. But as Shahrzad 's story progressed, as I fell deeper and deeper into a world of intrigue, secrets and lies, I was <b>bound</b>. To Shahrzad's fierceness, to Khalid's tragedy, to the sheer magic that engulfed me like it was a living and breathing thing. Because that's what I felt while reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath___the_Dawn__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath &amp; the Dawn (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</a>. <b>Alive</b>.<br><b>Enchanted</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1480196060ra/21283735.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‚ÄúYou have a beautiful laugh. Like the promise of tomorrow.‚Äù </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4600197.Renee_Ahdieh" title="Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Renee Ahdieh</a>'s writing is <b>exquisite</b>. Whether she described luscious palaces, delectable dishes and lavish clothes or a love so palpable that ripped your insides open, devastating truths or heartbreaking choices, she <b>captivated</b> you. She trapped you in a world painted in yellow, orange and red, a world where you could touch the sand and feel the heat burn your skin. She invaded your life and with her flying carpet made you a part of a <b>rich eastern culture</b>, a part of a <b>fairytale</b> you wished it would never end.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‚ÄúMy soul sees its equal in you.‚Äù </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Shahrzad was a fierce heroine, determined and stubborn, <i>a plague of a girl</i> that brought change to a lifeless palace. I was afraid that there would be love triangle drama that would ruin this remarkable reading experience, but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4600197.Renee_Ahdieh" title="Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Renee Ahdieh</a> knew exactly how to handle it. Yes, when Shahrzad married Khalid she was in love with another boy. But the connection, the trust and eventually the love that was built between the boy-king and his wife left no space for doubt that they belonged together. Khalid was prepared to kill Shahrzad. Shahrzad was prepared to kill Khalid. But none of them was prepared to find their equal, their perfect match, the air that filled their lungs. Their relationship would be angsty, sweet or painful, but the bond that was forged was unbreakable. And Khalid, oh my darling Khalid, he was a mystery, a troubled king with good intentions, aloof but caring, a <i>beautiful monster</i> I came to cherish deeply.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>‚ÄúThere is no one I would rather see the sunrise with than you.‚Äù</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>There is no one I would rather spend my precious free time with than Khalid, Shahrzad, Jalal and Despina. They made me smile, tear up and dream, travel and love, and for that I am forever indebted to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4600197.Renee_Ahdieh" title="Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">Renee Ahdieh</a>. If you haven't read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/18798983.The_Wrath___the_Dawn__The_Wrath___the_Dawn___1_" title="The Wrath &amp; the Dawn (The Wrath &amp; the Dawn, #1) by Renee Ahdieh" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</a> yet, don't waste another minute. A mesmerizing world of deception, curses and powerful feelings is waiting in the form of paper and words.<br><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/katerina_papas/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/KaterinaPapas" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/Booknest.eu/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="http://booknest.eu/index.php/component/k2/item/280-thewrathandthedawn" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6329006839360692249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1545837679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17328738347884579723"><b>
  <i>I will live to see tomorrow‚Äôs sunset. Make no mistake. I swear I will live to see as many sunsets as it takes. <br/>And I will kill you.<br/>With my own hands.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Here‚Äôs what happened: I was halfway through this book when I realized that it was slightly late, that the next day I would have to go to work early in the morning and that we humans need sleep in order to survive through the day. So, as a farewell to the book and because my curiosity took over, I decided to open the book at a random remaining pa</span>
  <span id="freeText17328738347884579723" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>I will live to see tomorrow‚Äôs sunset. Make no mistake. I swear I will live to see as many sunsets as it takes. <br />And I will kill you.<br />With my own hands.</i>
</b><br /><br />Here‚Äôs what happened: I was halfway through this book when I realized that it was slightly late, that the next day I would have to go to work early in the morning and that we humans need sleep in order to survive through the day. So, as a farewell to the book and because my curiosity took over, I decided to open the book at a random remaining page and read the first quote my eyes would lay on. <br /><br />Of course, it had to be <b>
  <i>that</i>
</b> quote. You know what I mean, the kind of sentence that you just feel would illustrate an important turning point in the story. You probably already know what I did next, don‚Äôt you? I couldn‚Äôt for the life of me stop there, even if I needed to, because I would not have been able to sleep with so many thoughts in my mind. And that‚Äôs how I finished this book in a single night. (Pssst, I‚Äôm glad you couldn‚Äôt see me the next morning.)<br /><br /><b>THAT SAYS A LOT.</b><br /><br />I personally don‚Äôt just go around sacrificing my sleep for any book. It has to be worth the tiredness, squinted eyes and overall grogginess we usually experience the next day. I regret nothing.<br /><br />Ahdieh, what did you do to me? Now I know I have to read her books in the daylight and if possible on a day without school or work. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin‚Äô</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_1663139872" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1663139872" />
    <a title="Riley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23179211-riley"><img alt="Riley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601446413p2/23179211.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1663139872?book_show_action=true">Jun 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Riley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Riley" href="/user/show/23179211-riley">Riley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23179211-riley?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23179211-riley?shelf=diverse-recs">diverse-recs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1663139872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7257919453344900264">Actual rating: 1.5<br/><br/>Do you ever just hear about a book and know without a shadow of a doubt that you will love it? That‚Äôs how I always felt about this book. I had seen rave review after rave review. Everyone I know LOVES it. So I always just knew that I would love it too. <br/><br/>I was wrong. <br/><br/>This book was painful to get through. From the forced writing style to the lackluster plot and flat characters. To say I am disappointed with this book is an understantment. <br/><br/>I know a lot of people praise the writing </span>
  <span id="freeText7257919453344900264" style="display:none">Actual rating: 1.5<br /><br />Do you ever just hear about a book and know without a shadow of a doubt that you will love it? That‚Äôs how I always felt about this book. I had seen rave review after rave review. Everyone I know LOVES it. So I always just knew that I would love it too. <br /><br />I was wrong. <br /><br />This book was painful to get through. From the forced writing style to the lackluster plot and flat characters. To say I am disappointed with this book is an understantment. <br /><br />I know a lot of people praise the writing style but for me it did not work. At all. I am all for flowery writing, but this went beyond that and actually took away from the story being written. I had a hard time seeing past metaphor after metaphor after metaphor. If I have to see the phrase ‚Äúflashing eyes‚Äù one more time I am going to scream. What does flashing eyes even mean?? Why are everyones eyes flashing?? All it did was build a wall between me and the story and caused me to feel no emotional connection to the characters. My biggest problem regarding the writing was the fact that she kept TELLING me things and not SHOWING them. <br /><br />Another thing that really bothered me about the writing was the use of foreign language. I fully appreciate that the author made an attempt to add foreign language to the book but she would just casually thrown these words in with absolutely zero context clues to decipher what the heck they mean. I had to constantly keep flipping to the back of the book and look up words in the glossary and every time I did it would stunt the flow of the book. <br /><br />Shazi was such an annoying main character. First of all, she volunteered to be the kings bride and willingly went to the palace with no plan as to how she would kill him and knowing nothing about him. Then as she is there she talks a big game in her head about killing him and getting revenge BUT SHE NEVER EVEN TRIES. And the one time she even thinks about doing it they end up making out instead. SERIOUSLY? Her thoughts and actions do not match up and that was so infuriating. <br /><br />Which leads me to the romance. Why do Shazi and Khalid like each other? When did their love happen? Did they meet of page and develop this relationship because it sure as hell didn‚Äôt happen on page. One second Shazi wants to murder him and get vengeance for him murdering her best friend and the next page she is talking about her fluttering heart. Seriously? TWO DAYS! Two days is all it took for her to fall for her friends murderer. <br /><br />And as for her friend, we never see their friendship. So I don‚Äôt get the emotions behind Shazi wanting revenge. I don‚Äôt care her friend died. I don‚Äôt feel the feels. If there was just one scene of her and Shiva I would have understood more, but alas we were just TOLD they were friends and not SHOWN. <br /><br />The only character I cared about in the slightest was Shazi‚Äôs bodyguard who never spoke. Other than him I couldn‚Äôt care less about these characters and their problems. Until about page 340 nothing happened in this book plot wise. It was just chapter after chapter of Shazi having conversations in her bedroom. <br /><br />For as much as I didn‚Äôt like this book, I will be reading the sequel. Maybe not anytime soon, but I need to know if it gets better. I‚Äôm really hoping it does. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7257919453344900264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1175057480" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1175057480" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1175057480?book_show_action=true">Jan 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=badass-females">badass-females</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1175057480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2795862420499973981"><i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i> is every recently amazing YA book thrown into one read.<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1088241075?book_show_action=false' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'> <i>Red Queen</i></a> meets <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1181149413?book_show_action=false' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>An Ember in the Ashes</i>
</a> meets <a href='http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/2015/05/a-court-of-thorns-and-roses-by-sarah-j.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <i>A Court of Thorns and Roses</i>
</a>. The main difference it has between those books is the amount of action. <i>The Wrath </i>definitely set aside action packed scenes for a slower more lyrical literature depth.<br/><br/>Sharhrzad (Shazi) is out to seek revenge for the murder of her best friend and decides too volunteer to be the next wife of the Caliph of Khorasan. The Caliph is known for b</span>
  <span id="freeText2795862420499973981" style="display:none"><i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i> is every recently amazing YA book thrown into one read.<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1088241075?book_show_action=false" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"> <i>Red Queen</i></a> meets <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1181149413?book_show_action=false" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>An Ember in the Ashes</i>
</a> meets <a href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/2015/05/a-court-of-thorns-and-roses-by-sarah-j.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <i>A Court of Thorns and Roses</i>
</a>. The main difference it has between those books is the amount of action. <i>The Wrath </i>definitely set aside action packed scenes for a slower more lyrical literature depth.<br><br>Sharhrzad (Shazi) is out to seek revenge for the murder of her best friend and decides too volunteer to be the next wife of the Caliph of Khorasan. The Caliph is known for being ruthless, heartless, and cruel. But the thing he is most known for is the fact that every day he takes a different wife and every following dawn he kills her. Shazi doesn‚Äôt care why the king does this she only cares about righting what has been wrong and insuring that this fate doesn‚Äôt come to another girl.Since this is told from a 3rd person point of view us as reading know that there is clearly more to the story than meets the eye. As Shazi gets to know Khalid (The Caliph) she learns he is not what she thought he was. She beings to become conflicted between doing what she set out to do and listening to her heart. Things only get more complicated when Shazi pre suicide mission boyfriend, Tariq, sets out to get her back.<br><br>I'm usually am not the biggest fan of the 3rd person pov but in this case I found myself falling in love with it. That was not the only thing I fell for, the characters won me over. Shazi is our leading lady and the character I connected most with. Having to see her go back and forth on what she should do had me struggling along with her. She is a fierce lead and her silver tongued attitude is a forced to be reckoned with. Her take no crap ways and honesty will win you over. Can't help but love a girl with so much street smarts. Khalid is our leading male and I can‚Äôt express enough how much I loved his character. He isn‚Äôt a man of <br>many words, and the ones he uses he chooses wisely, time and time again <br>had me swooning. Though I connected more with Shazi without a doubt Khalid was my favorite character. He has definitely made his way onto my list of fictional book boyfriends. I loved the mystery surrounding him, his intelligence, and his ability to read people. This is also the only negative feedback I have on the book. The romance, though amazing, I wanted more of it. I wanted more ‚Äúscreen time‚Äù with Shazi and Khalid. The moments we get with them are so perfect that it made me want this book to be longer. I think it says a lot if your only real complaint is that something was so good you wanted more of it. This is a very <br>very minor issue in the grand scheme of things.¬† Both Shazi and Khalid are complex and well built characters. The fact that we are given so much back story and tells from their childhoods also gave these characters something that a lot of other books miss. Tariq is the only character I felt I didn‚Äôt really connect with or understand in this book. though I see his value and what he brings to the table I just think Khalid won me over and had it so I wasn't even glancing Tariq way.<br><br><div>
<br><b><i>‚ÄúLove is a force unto itself, sayyidi. For love, people consider the unthinkable...and often achieve the impossible. I would not sneer at its power.‚Äù¬†¬†</i></b><br><br>As I stated above <i>The Wrath</i> is a book that can be compare to others that have been released lately but it has something so different to it. Though most of it's action packed scenes are left towards till the end of the story, Renee's writing had it so I was still on the edge of my seat either way. She manages keeps a steady pace throughout the whole novel. Renee's writing is so beautiful and gripping. The brilliance behind how she survives through the night is what got me so hooked right away and every wonderful sentence after kept me there. This novel brought a whole new meaning to stories having power. Waiting so long to give us the true answer to the riddle yet giving us little bits and pieces really worked so well for this book. The action scenes in this book are perfectly placed along with their delivery.<br><br><b><i>The Wrath and the Dawn</i> surpassed any expectation I had for this book. It brings something so new and diverse to this genre while still managing to fit in so well. The perfect start to a series. It‚Äôs a fresh retelling with and amazing band of characters, perfect amount of romance, and the perfect mystery surrounding it. Finding out this is the first book and that there will be a sequel has me beyond giddy!<br><br><br><div>
<br><a href="http://2.bp.blogspot.com/-4hzOgRMKuLg/VYcQT8mHSCI/AAAAAAAAB2w/lsTyANhoFyY/s1600/twatd.gif" rel="nofollow noopener"><img height="179" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1434915330ra/15277967.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>
</div>
<br><br><br><br><b>READ THIS REVIEW AND OTHERS OVER ON OUR BLOG: <br><br><a href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Southern Bred Souther Read </a><br><br><a href="http://southernbredsouthernread.blogspot.com/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Southern Bred Souther Read </a><br><br><br>Originally read- may 2015<br>Re read- March 2016</b></b>
</div></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1558854503?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nat" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nat" href="/user/show/23381142-nat">Nat</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/23381142-nat?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1558854503" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13103991497361050492"><i>‚ÄúI‚Äôve been told a good storyteller can trap an audience with a single sentence.‚Äù</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456414404ra/18232184.gif' width='320' height='210' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br/><br/>I picked this book up completely on a whim, and I‚Äôm so glad that I did. I was completely entranced by <b>The Wrath & the Dawn</b>. The setting was just right, the writing was engaging, and I thought every character brought something important to the story. This book felt like it should go on forever, and I was really disappointed when it didn't. <br/><br/><b>The Wrath & the Dawn</b> follows Shahrzad on a ques</span>
  <span id="freeText13103991497361050492" style="display:none"><i>‚ÄúI‚Äôve been told a good storyteller can trap an audience with a single sentence.‚Äù</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456414404ra/18232184.gif" width="320" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>This review contains <b>*spoilers*</b>.<br><br>I picked this book up completely on a whim, and I‚Äôm so glad that I did. I was completely entranced by <b>The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</b>. The setting was just right, the writing was engaging, and I thought every character brought something important to the story. This book felt like it should go on forever, and I was really disappointed when it didn't. <br><br><b>The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</b> follows Shahrzad on a quest to avenge the death of her dearest friend, Shiva. Her friend was executed at dawn by Khalid, the eighteen-year-old Caliph of Khorasan. Each night he takes a new bride only to have a silk cord wrapped around her throat come morning. Shahrzad is determined to stay alive.<br><br><i>‚ÄúYou said you understood; your life is forfeit. That was clear from the very beginning.‚Äù<br>Shahrzad rose to her full height. She pulled back her shoulders and lifted her elfin chin.<br>When she spoke, she matched the biting softness in his tone.<br>‚ÄúAll our lives are forfeit, sayyidi. It is just a question of when. And I would like one more day.‚Äù</i><br><br>The slow romance that developed between Shahrzad and Khalid had me on the edge of my seat. I <s>needed</s> wanted them to KISS already. <br><br><i>‚ÄúYou were saying?‚Äù He was so close, his words were more breath than sound.<br>‚ÄúHow‚Äîhow dare you say that to me?‚Äù she whispered.<br>His eyes glittered with something akin to amusement.<br>‚ÄúHow dare I imply you caused this mess?‚Äù<br>‚ÄúMe? This is not my fault! This is your fault!‚Äù<br>‚ÄúMine?‚Äù<br>‚ÄúYou and your temper, Khalid!‚Äù<br>‚ÄúNo. You and your mouth, Shazi.‚Äù<br>‚ÄúWrong, you wretched lout!‚Äù<br>‚ÄúSee? That mouth.‚Äù He reached up and grazed his thumb across her lips. ‚ÄúThat‚Äîmagnificent mouth.‚Äù</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1420781351ra/13261471.gif" width="320" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>When they finally did kiss, it was heartwarming and heartbreaking. This is the first book in a long time that has managed to make me feel so many emotions all at once. <br>I knew what Khalid was, <i>a <s>beautiful</s> monster</i>, but he had this perfect way with words and he was so sweet with Shazi and and and...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456414936ra/18232370.gif" width="320" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>‚ÄúHow can I desire him? After he killed Shiva? After he killed so many young girls, without explanation?<br>What‚Äôs wrong with me?‚Äù</i><br>I felt just as perplexed as Shahrzad, but Khalid was so good that it hurt me. My favorite parts of this book were always with the two of them together.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456406479ra/18230677.gif" width="320" height="210" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But he‚Äôs not the monster everyone perceives him to be, he‚Äôs just a boy with secrets. <i>‚ÄúJust one boy and one girl.‚Äù</i><br>And when Shahrzad found his letters of apology to the families of the girls murdered at dawn, especially the letter addressed to Shiva‚Äôs family, I had tears streaming down my face.<br>This book is too good.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456414404ra/18232185.gif" width="330" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I also really cared about the secondary characters, they all added something special to the story.<br>The friendship between Despina and Shazi reminded me somehow of Cinder and Iko‚Äôs friendship, which I truly enjoyed. They made me smile with their daily conversations.<br>And Jalal had me laughing every single time he opened his mouth. <br><br><i>‚ÄúWould you be willing to teach me how to use a bow and arrow, Captain al-Khoury?‚Äù she asked.<br>‚ÄúThat depends on a few things. The first being that you dispense with the formalities and just call me Jalal. The second being that Khalid never discover my part in this transgression.‚Äù<br>Khalid? He calls him by his first name?<br>‚ÄúI can meet those terms. Gladly. If you‚Äôll return the gesture, on both parts.‚Äù<br>‚ÄúJalal leaned forward conspiratorially. ‚ÄúThen follow me, Jalal.‚Äù<br>Shahrzad laughed.‚Äù</i><br><br>I really hope we‚Äôll get to see more of Jalal and Despina together in the next book.<br><br>But I‚Äôm not quite sure how I feel about Tariq‚Äî I definitely didn‚Äôt want him to be with Shahrzad‚Äî whenever he did try to persuade her to be with him, I got really mad. <br>There‚Äôs just something about him that I don‚Äôt quite like. I can‚Äôt seem to put my finger on what exactly. He reminded me a bit of Adam from the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/65730-shatter-me" rel="nofollow noopener">Shatter Me Series</a>. <br>So there‚Äôs currently more hate than love in my feelings towards Tariq. He frustrated me a lot (especially towards the end).<br><br><i>‚ÄúI know this isn‚Äôt you. I know something must have happened. But we can fix it. I can fix it. Come home with me. Every day we are apart is a day closer to death. A day wasted on what might have been. I can‚Äôt stomach it any longer. Come home.‚Äù<br>‚ÄúBut,‚Äù she whispered, ‚ÄúI am home.‚Äù</i><br>(I was so relieved when Shazi told him that.)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1456416171ra/18232542.gif" width="320" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>All I can think of right now is that I need the sequel. <br>This story is captivating, beautiful, and definitely a favorite of mine. I can‚Äôt believe it‚Äôs over. I <s>want</s> need more. <br><br><i>*Note: I'm an Amazon Affiliate. If you're interested in buying</i> <b>The Wrath &amp; the Dawn</b>, <i>just click on the image below to go through my link.         <div class="reviewText stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer13359714858341222322"><b>HELLO. I AM NOT OKAY. THIS BOOK IS A BILLION PERCENT INCREDIBLE AND AJKLFDSAQTQEQQQQQJKLQ.</b> Words?! WHAT WORDS. I'm just absolutely dancing from the proverbial rooftops that I fell in love with this book. I've had <i>such</i> a slack year for reading. All my highly anticipated reads have splattered like mayonnaise on the wall. But this?! <b>They hype is completely justified.</b> It's beautiful and visual and delicious (seriously, so much delicious food) and the characters were absolute <i>perfection</i>. I cannot rig</span>
  <span id="freeText13359714858341222322" style="display:none"><b>HELLO. I AM NOT OKAY. THIS BOOK IS A BILLION PERCENT INCREDIBLE AND AJKLFDSAQTQEQQQQQJKLQ.</b> Words?! WHAT WORDS. I'm just absolutely dancing from the proverbial rooftops that I fell in love with this book. I've had <i>such</i> a slack year for reading. All my highly anticipated reads have splattered like mayonnaise on the wall. But this?! <b>They hype is completely justified.</b> It's beautiful and visual and delicious (seriously, so much delicious food) and the characters were absolute <i>perfection</i>. I cannot right now. I CANNOT. I AM JUST SO HAPPY I LOVED IT SO MUCH. <br /><br />Ahem.<br /><br />Okay, but let's scroll backwards a little and <b>let me tell you the story of how I have history with this story.</b> When I was 12 I was obsessed with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/238460.Shadow_Spinner" title="Shadow Spinner by Susan Fletcher" rel="nofollow noopener">Shadow Spinner</a>. It was the book of my LIFE. I reread it nine trillion times and pledge to myself I would write a retelling of Shahrazad one day. THEN I SAW THIS BOOK WAS COMING OUT. I was half disappointed (dang, I missed my opportunity) and half elated because I GET TO RELIVE MY CHILDHOOD LOVE. I'm <i>so grateful</i> The Wrath and the Dawn really stuck to the original story and embellished it beautiful and in a more YA way (Shadow Spinner is, obviously, a children's book). I had mega high expectations: AND I WAS NOT LET DOWN. <br /><br /><b>So it's a fantasy, but with a pinch of magic and a <i>lot</i> of Persian culture.</b> I love this. I ADORE THIS. I kind of wished it had been an historical fantasy? But the magic was very subtle and while it impacted the finale, it wasn't like "OH SUDDENLY WE CAN MAGIC GENIES OUT OF LAMPS." Although there was hints of a magic carpet?! I really hope they do something fantastic with that. But omg, the food! THE FOOD. I love books that use food to its full glory. It slips in culture <i>and</i> it's freaking delicious to read about. I nearly died of starvation just reading the foodie descriptions. Basically this book gets a whole extra star for FOOD.<br /><blockquote>...setting plates of food in front of each guest -- aromatic rice with fresh dill and split fava beans, lamb simmered in sauce of turmeric and caramelized onions, skewers of chicken and roasted tomatoes, fresh vegetables garnished with mint and chopped parsley, olives marinated in fine oil, lavash bread with rounds of goat cheese and seemingly endless sweet preserves...(pg 252)</blockquote><br />Excuse me while I die. This is beautiful. This is art. Yum.<br /><br />And of course the rest of the description was JUST as perfect as this. <b>Okay, just all of the writing was beautiful and brilliant.</b> It was sharp, edgy writing. Every word MATTERED. And the sentences were short and biting. When it used detailed description, it went for words that packed a punch. And the outfits?! AFJDKL THEY WERE BEAUTIFUL. <b>It's also narrated by a LOT of people</b>. I loved this. I love fantasy that comes from more than one POV. The most important one, obviously, is Shahrzad's. But we get to see from Khalid (the monster boy-king) from Jalal (his cousin) and from Tariq (the childhood sweetheart) and even the father (who possibly is insane, jury's out). I liked how this rounded out the story SO MUCH. <br /><br /><b>And a quick peek at the characters?!</b> Because I am in love with them. IN LOVE. I SHIP MY SHIP SO HARD I MIGHT EXPLODE. *ships aggressively*<br /><b>+ Shahrzad:</b> She was so small and sassy and had a big mouth and a sharp wit. I LOVED HER. She reminded me of Celaena Sardothien from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Throne of Glass</a> but with less viciousness. Shahrzad could be sweet...if she wanted to. BUT HER SPUNK. She was a billion percent awesome.<br /><b>+ Khalid:</b> Ah, the monster-boy-king. So, since he kills a girl every night, he's got to be EVIL, right?!! WELL. I figured there'd be more to that story than meets the eye. I figured there'd be a horrifying truth that made it okay. And I was basically right. So I got on Khalid's side pretty fast...because omg, he's adorable. He's angry and violent BUT ADORABLE. He's unwanted and he's been abused. (Hello, his father <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[murdered his mother <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> in front of 6-year-old Khalid THAT IS KINDA DAMAGING.) I ship him and Shahrzad so so hard I possibly might explode.<br /><b>+ Jalal:</b> He's Khalid's cousin and next commander-of-the-guard. He was sort of smooth and slick and sassy, and his relationship with Khalid was "I WANNA BE FRIENDS" while Khalid is like "GET AWAY FROM ME I AM A MEANIE". So they were adorable. Everything is adorable, dammit.<br /><b>+ Depsina</b>: OMG I LOVE HER MORE THAN WORDS CAN SAY. She's the handmaiden, and so sassy. She's also plump and downright gorgeous and can do her makeup like a dream and has a mega crush on Jalal. Qjfadsklqouqqqq I love her. She gives Shahrzad so. much. lip. It's amazing and their friendship is one of my favourite things.<br /><b>+ Tariq</b>: UGH I HATE TARIQ. I was terrified when he was introduced and started his campaign to get Shahrzad back because I HATE LOVE TRIANGLES WITH A FIERY PASSION. They are hellish. So there <i>is</i> sort of a triangle, but Shahrzad doesn't spend the entire book trying to choose between two boys, thank the bookish heavens. But Tariq was brash and violent and didn't ever LISTEN. he didn't even care what Shahrzad wanted, just that <i>he</i> wanted her. That ain't love. But I <i>love</i> how the book calls him out on this:<br /><blockquote>"Why do you love her?"<br />"Because --" Tariq rubbed at the back of his neck. "All of my most cherished memories are of her. I've suffered alongside her. And...we've laughed at nothing together."<br />Omar's hand fell from Tariq's shoulder. "A shared history does not entitle you to a future, my friend."</blockquote><br />Bless the ground Omar stands on. HE IS A WISE MORTAL. <br />Ahem.<br /><br /><b>OH OH HOW COULD I FORGET TO TALK ABOUT THE STORY ASPECT?!!</b> As you (might) know, the original tale of Shahrazad is about a girl who is married to a Sultan who slays his bride every night. But Shahrazad tells a story and it lasts past the dawn and then she cuts off, and, in order to hear the rest, the sultan has to let her life. OKAY SO THE WRATH AND THE DAWN TOTALLY DID THIS YAY!. But possibly my only squinty-ness is because there isn't that much emphasis on the stories. It's in the first 50% of the book, and then basically extinct in the last. This saddens me. But there WERE stories, so I won't complain too much.<br /><br /><b>And the romance?!</b> IT WAS PERFECT. I HAVE EXACTLY ZERO COMPLAINTS BECAUSE IT'S GORGEOUS AND BEAUTIFUL. AND I SHIP IT SO HARD I CAN ONLY SHRIEK. It was a slow attraction and it was so sweet, and Khalid was just bursting with this absolutely incredible soliloquies at the end. Omg. There goes my heart. <br /><br /><b>Basically it is the most perfect book in the universe.</b> It was everything I wanted. The writing was DELICIOUS. And the characters all stole my heart and I would read nine thousand books about them. Persian fantasies have such a special place in my heart. AND THEN THERE WAS ALL THAT GOOD FOOD. That helped. It did, I won't lie. So if you're torn about trying this: jUST READ IT. I'M GONNA JUST GO WAIL BECAUSE THE ENDING WAS SO HEART RENDING AND I HAVE TO WAIT A WHOLE YEAR FOR BOOK 2. *hyperventilates*<br /><br />*** <br /><br /><blockquote>Khalid had to answer for such vile deeds. Such rampant deaths.<br />Even if he was her air.<br />Even if she loved him beyond words.</blockquote><br /><blockquote>One hundred lives for the one you took. One life to one dawn. Should you fail but a single morn, I will take from you your dreams. I shall take from you your city. And I shall take from you these lives, a thousandfold.</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="13359714858341222322" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
